Each artificial neuron has one or more numerical inputs and produces a single numerical output.[[115]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-Abbod2007-115) To find the output of a neuron, we take the (weighted) sum of all the neuron's inputs, [weighted](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Weight_function "Weight function") by the _weights_ of the _connections_ from each of those inputs. We then add a _bias_ term to this sum.[[116]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-DAWSON1998-116) This weighted sum (plus the bias) is then passed through a nonlinear [activation function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Activation_function "Activation function") to produce the neuron's output.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:5-117)[[118]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-118)[[119]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-119)

To create a neural network, multiple artificial neurons are connected together, with the outputs of some neurons being fed into the input of others. The inputs to the initial _input neurons_ are external data, such as images and text (encoded as a series of numbers). The outputs of the final _output neurons_ correspond to the task the network was created to do, such as recognizing an object in an image.[[117]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:5-117)

### Organization

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=13 "Edit section: Organization")]

[![Image 13](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Neural_Network.svg/250px-Neural_Network.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Neural_Network.svg)

Structure of a feedforward neural network with four layers

The neurons are typically organized into multiple layers, especially in deep learning. The layer that receives external data is the _input layer_, and the layer that produces the ultimate result is the _output layer_. In between them are zero or more _hidden layers_. Single layer and unlayered networks are also used.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

Between two layers, multiple connection patterns are possible. Traditionally, they are _fully connected_, with every neuron in one layer connecting to every neuron in the next layer.[[120]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-120) However, in [convolutional neural networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convolutional_neural_network "Convolutional neural network"), some layers are _convolutional,_ meaning each neuron in the next layer is connected to a set of spatially grouped neurons in the previous layer.[[121]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-flexible-121)[[122]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-122)[_[clarification needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Please\_clarify "Wikipedia:Please clarify")_]

In most neural networks,[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_] the outputs of the neurons in one layer are only connected to the inputs of neurons in the immediately following layer (forming a [directed acyclic graph](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Directed_acyclic_graph "Directed acyclic graph")), meaning information can only flow "forward" from one layer to the next. These are known as [_feedforward networks_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Feedforward_neural_network "Feedforward neural network").[[123]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-Zell1994p73-123) In contrast, networks that allow connections between neurons in the same or previous layers are known as [_recurrent networks_](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Recurrent_neural_network "Recurrent neural network").[[124]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-124)

## Learning

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=14 "Edit section: Learning")]

![Image 14](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png)This section includes a [list of references](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources"), [related reading](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Further_reading "Wikipedia:Further reading"), or [external links](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links "Wikipedia:External links"), **but its sources remain unclear because it lacks [inline citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")**. Please help [improve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Fact_and_Reference_Check "Wikipedia:WikiProject Fact and Reference Check") this section by [introducing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:When_to_cite "Wikipedia:When to cite") more precise citations._(August 2019)_ _([Learn how and when to remove this message](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Maintenance\_template\_removal "Help:Maintenance template removal"))_

See also: [Mathematical optimization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_optimization "Mathematical optimization"), [Estimation theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Estimation_theory "Estimation theory"), and [Machine learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning "Machine learning")

The function of a neural network is defined by its architecture – how the different neurons are organized and connected to one another – and the values, or _weights_, associated with each of the neurons, determining how it calculates its output based on its input connections.[[125]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-125)[[note 1]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-126) The goal of learning involves adjusting the weights (and optional thresholds) of the network to improve the accuracy of the result. This is done by minimizing the observed errors among sample observations.

Neural networks are typically trained through [empirical risk minimization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Empirical_risk_minimization "Empirical risk minimization"), which is based on the idea of optimizing the network's parameters to minimize the difference, or empirical risk, between the predicted output and the actual target values in a given dataset.[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:2-127) Gradient-based methods such as [backpropagation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backpropagation "Backpropagation") are usually used to estimate the parameters of the network.[[126]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:2-127) During the training phase, ANNs learn from [labeled](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Labeled_data "Labeled data") training data by iteratively updating their parameters to minimize a defined [loss function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loss_functions_for_classification "Loss functions for classification").[[94]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:4-94) This method allows the network to generalize to unseen data.

Practically this is done by defining a [loss function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loss_function "Loss function")[[note 2]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-128) that is evaluated periodically during learning. As long as its output continues to decline, learning continues. The cost is frequently defined as a [statistic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistic "Statistic") whose value can only be approximated. The outputs are actually numbers, so when the error is low, the difference between the output (almost certainly a cat) and the correct answer (cat) is small. Learning attempts to reduce the total of the differences across the observations. Most learning models can be viewed as a straightforward application of [optimization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_optimization "Mathematical optimization") theory and [statistical estimation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_estimation "Statistical estimation").[[113]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-Zell1994ch5.2-113)[[127]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-129)

Learning is typically considered complete when examining additional observations does not usefully reduce the error rate. Even after learning, the error rate typically does not reach 0. If after learning, the error rate is too high, the network typically must be redesigned.

### Loss function

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=15 "Edit section: Loss function")]

[![Image 15: [icon]](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg)This section **needs expansion** with: Talk more about how loss functions are described, what types exist for different problems. You can help by [adding missing information](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=). _(March 2026)_

While it is possible to define a loss function [ad hoc](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ad_hoc "Ad hoc"), frequently the choice is determined by the function's desirable properties (such as [convexity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convex_function "Convex function"), differentiability, and [robustness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robustness_(computer_science) "Robustness (computer science)")) [[128]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-130) because it arises from the model (e.g. in a probabilistic model, the model's [posterior probability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Posterior_probability "Posterior probability") can be used as an inverse cost).[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

### Backpropagation

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=16 "Edit section: Backpropagation")]

Main article: [Backpropagation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Backpropagation "Backpropagation")

Backpropagation is a method used to adjust the connection weights to compensate for each error found during learning. The error amount is effectively divided among the connections. Technically, backpropagation calculates the [gradient](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gradient "Gradient") (the derivative) of the [loss function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Loss_function "Loss function") associated with a given state with respect to the weights. The weight updates can be done via stochastic gradient descent or other methods, such as _[extreme learning machines](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Extreme\_learning\_machine "Extreme learning machine")_,[[129]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-131) "no-prop" networks,[[130]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-132) training without backtracking,[[131]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-133) "weightless" networks,[[132]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-RBMTRAIN-134)[[133]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-135) and [non-connectionist neural networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Holographic_associative_memory "Holographic associative memory").[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

### Hyperparameters

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=17 "Edit section: Hyperparameters")]

Main article: [Hyperparameter (machine learning)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperparameter_(machine_learning) "Hyperparameter (machine learning)")

A [hyperparameter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hyperparameter_(machine_learning) "Hyperparameter (machine learning)") is a [parameter](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Parameter "Parameter") defining any configurable part of the learning process, whose value is set prior to training.[[134]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-136) Examples of hyperparameters include [learning rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Learning_rate "Learning rate"), batch size and regularization parameters.[[135]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-137) The performance of a neural network is strongly influenced by the choice of hyperparameter values, and thus the hyperparameters are often optimized as part of the training process, a process called hyperparameter tuning or hyperparameter optimization.[[136]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-138)

#### Learning rate

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=18 "Edit section: Learning rate")]

Main article: [Learning rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Learning_rate "Learning rate")

The learning rate defines the size of the corrective steps that the model takes to adjust for errors in each observation.[[137]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-139) A high learning rate shortens the training time, but with lower ultimate accuracy, while a lower learning rate takes longer, but with the potential for greater accuracy. Optimizations such as [Quickprop](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quickprop "Quickprop") are primarily aimed at speeding up error minimization, while other improvements mainly try to increase reliability. In order to avoid [oscillation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Oscillation "Oscillation") inside the network such as alternating connection weights, and to improve the rate of convergence, refinements use an [adaptive learning rate](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptive_learning_rate "Adaptive learning rate") that increases or decreases as appropriate.[[138]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-140) The concept of momentum allows the balance between the gradient and the previous change to be weighted such that the weight adjustment depends to some degree on the previous change. A momentum close to 0 emphasizes the gradient, while a value close to 1 emphasizes the last change.[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

### Learning paradigms

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=19 "Edit section: Learning paradigms")]

![Image 16](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png)This section includes a [list of references](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources"), [related reading](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Further_reading "Wikipedia:Further reading"), or [external links](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links "Wikipedia:External links"), **but its sources remain unclear because it lacks [inline citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")**. Please help [improve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Fact_and_Reference_Check "Wikipedia:WikiProject Fact and Reference Check") this section by [introducing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:When_to_cite "Wikipedia:When to cite") more precise citations._(August 2019)_ _([Learn how and when to remove this message](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Maintenance\_template\_removal "Help:Maintenance template removal"))_

Machine learning is commonly separated into three main learning paradigms, [supervised learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervised_learning "Supervised learning"),[[139]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-141)[unsupervised learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unsupervised_learning "Unsupervised learning")[[140]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-142) and [reinforcement learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning "Reinforcement learning").[[141]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-143) Each corresponds to a particular learning task.

#### Supervised learning

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Supervised learning")]

[Supervised learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Supervised_learning "Supervised learning") uses a set of paired inputs and desired outputs. The learning task is to produce the desired output for each input. In this case, the cost function is related to eliminating incorrect deductions.[[142]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-144) A commonly used cost is the [mean-squared error](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean-squared_error "Mean-squared error"), which tries to minimize the average squared error between the network's output and the desired output. Tasks suited for supervised learning are [pattern recognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_recognition "Pattern recognition") (also known as classification) and [regression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regression_analysis "Regression analysis") (also known as function approximation). Supervised learning is also applicable to sequential data (e.g., for handwriting, speech and [gesture recognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gesture_recognition "Gesture recognition")). This can be thought of as learning with a "teacher", in the form of a function that provides continuous feedback on the quality of solutions obtained thus far.

#### Unsupervised learning

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Unsupervised learning")]

In [unsupervised learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unsupervised_learning "Unsupervised learning"), input data is given along with the cost function, some function of the data {\displaystyle \textstyle x}![Image 17: {\displaystyle \textstyle x}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1bd1c9e87a24e459706fa8e63b9e5d94db4540b4) and the network's output. The cost function is dependent on the task (the model domain) and any _[a priori](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/A\_priori\_and\_a\_posteriori "A priori and a posteriori")_ assumptions (the implicit properties of the model, its parameters and the observed variables). As a trivial example, consider the model {\displaystyle \textstyle f(x)=a}![Image 18: {\displaystyle \textstyle f(x)=a}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a0e4cc2a7c5c4f65d59b669d64c7759623c648c5) where {\displaystyle \textstyle a}![Image 19: {\displaystyle \textstyle a}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7abc4e8a2ef67ff9b7ad050afa4cf286c3ec0cd3) is a constant and the cost {\displaystyle \textstyle C=E[(x-f(x))^{2}]}![Image 20: {\displaystyle \textstyle C=E[(x-f(x))^{2}]}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/2929ecb1606fdfeaddc55477d9671e11c034e21c). Minimizing this cost produces a value of {\displaystyle \textstyle a}![Image 21: {\displaystyle \textstyle a}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7abc4e8a2ef67ff9b7ad050afa4cf286c3ec0cd3) that is equal to the mean of the data. The cost function can be much more complicated. Its form depends on the application: for example, in [compression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_compression "Data compression") it could be related to the [mutual information](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mutual_information "Mutual information") between {\displaystyle \textstyle x}![Image 22: {\displaystyle \textstyle x}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1bd1c9e87a24e459706fa8e63b9e5d94db4540b4) and {\displaystyle \textstyle f(x)}![Image 23: {\displaystyle \textstyle f(x)}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e0fa998ae55408f7f94d08ee08a04fcf92330878), whereas in statistical modeling, it could be related to the [posterior probability](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Posterior_probability "Posterior probability") of the model given the data (note that in both of those examples, those quantities would be maximized rather than minimized). Tasks that fall within the paradigm of unsupervised learning are in general [estimation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Approximation "Approximation") problems; the applications include [clustering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_clustering "Data clustering"), the estimation of [statistical distributions](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Statistical_distributions "Statistical distributions"), [compression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_compression "Data compression") and [filtering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayesian_spam_filtering "Bayesian spam filtering").

#### Reinforcement learning

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Reinforcement learning")]

Main article: [Reinforcement learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning "Reinforcement learning")

See also: [Stochastic control](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_control "Stochastic control")

In applications such as playing video games, an actor takes a string of actions, receiving a generally unpredictable response from the environment after each one. The goal is to win the game, i.e., generate the most positive (lowest cost) responses. In [reinforcement learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Reinforcement_learning "Reinforcement learning"), the aim is to weight the network (devise a policy) to perform actions that minimize long-term (expected cumulative) cost. At each point in time the agent performs an action and the environment generates an observation and an [instantaneous](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Instant "Instant") cost, according to some (usually unknown) rules. The rules and the long-term cost usually only can be estimated. At any juncture, the agent decides whether to explore new actions to uncover their costs or to exploit prior learning to proceed more quickly.

Formally, the environment is modeled as a [Markov decision process](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markov_decision_process "Markov decision process") (MDP) with states {\displaystyle \textstyle {s_{1},...,s_{n}}\in S}![Image 24: {\displaystyle \textstyle {s_{1},...,s_{n}}\in S}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/594ab196af08f0326623318ae24ea08359f03c2f) and actions {\displaystyle \textstyle {a_{1},...,a_{m}}\in A}![Image 25: {\displaystyle \textstyle {a_{1},...,a_{m}}\in A}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c1a2b52db3ad57568da895b2171c90ae6e0de377). Because the state transitions are not known, probability distributions are used instead: the instantaneous cost distribution {\displaystyle \textstyle P(c_{t}|s_{t})}![Image 26: {\displaystyle \textstyle P(c_{t}|s_{t})}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d64a75ad0caf0be43f971b53a2c16b637bf8bb20), the observation distribution {\displaystyle \textstyle P(x_{t}|s_{t})}![Image 27: {\displaystyle \textstyle P(x_{t}|s_{t})}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/591cc95a2eb71b92b0fc200675bc8037094a37f0) and the transition distribution {\displaystyle \textstyle P(s_{t+1}|s_{t},a_{t})}![Image 28: {\displaystyle \textstyle P(s_{t+1}|s_{t},a_{t})}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0200f5e1c5ad6c6114027fd0f660399c8b584d71), while a policy is defined as the conditional distribution over actions given the observations. Taken together, the two define a [Markov chain](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Markov_chain "Markov chain") (MC). The aim is to discover the lowest-cost MC.

ANNs serve as the learning component in such applications.[[143]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-145)[[144]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-146)[Dynamic programming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dynamic_programming "Dynamic programming") coupled with ANNs (giving [neurodynamic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_oscillation "Neural oscillation") programming)[[145]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-147) has been applied to problems such as those involved in [vehicle routing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vehicle_routing "Vehicle routing"),[[146]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-148) video games, [natural resource management](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_resource_management "Natural resource management")[[147]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-149)[[148]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-150) and [medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medicine "Medicine")[[149]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-151) because of ANNs ability to mitigate losses of accuracy even when reducing the [discretization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Discretization "Discretization") grid density for numerically approximating the solution of control problems. Tasks that fall within the paradigm of reinforcement learning are control problems, [games](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Game "Game") and other sequential decision making tasks.

#### Self-learning

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Self-learning")]

Self-learning in neural networks was introduced in 1982 along with a neural network capable of self-learning named _crossbar adaptive array_ (CAA).[[150]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-152) It is a system with only one input, situation s, and only one output, action (or behavior) a. It has neither external advice input nor external reinforcement input from the environment. The CAA computes, in a crossbar fashion, both decisions about actions and emotions (feelings) about encountered situations. The system is driven by the interaction between cognition and emotion.[[151]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-153) Given the memory matrix, W =||w(a,s)||, the crossbar self-learning algorithm in each iteration performs the following computation:

 In situation s perform action a;
 Receive consequence situation s';
 Compute emotion of being in consequence situation v(s');
 Update crossbar memory w'(a,s) = w(a,s) + v(s').

The backpropagated value (secondary reinforcement) is the emotion toward the consequence situation. The CAA exists in two environments, one is behavioral environment where it behaves, and the other is genetic environment, where from it receives initial emotions (only once) about to be encountered situations in the behavioral environment. Having received the genome vector (species vector) from the genetic environment, the CAA will learn a goal-seeking behavior, in the behavioral environment that contains both desirable and undesirable situations.[[152]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-154)

#### Neuroevolution

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Neuroevolution")]

Main article: [Neuroevolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroevolution "Neuroevolution")

[Neuroevolution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neuroevolution "Neuroevolution") can create neural network topologies and weights using [evolutionary computation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_computation "Evolutionary computation"). It is competitive with sophisticated gradient descent approaches.[[153]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-155)[[154]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-156) One advantage of neuroevolution is that it may be less prone to get caught in "dead ends".[[155]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-157)

### Stochastic neural network

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Stochastic neural network")]

**Stochastic neural networks** originating from [Sherrington–Kirkpatrick models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spin_glass#Sherrington%E2%80%93Kirkpatrick_model "Spin glass") are a type of artificial neural network built by introducing random variations into the network, either by giving the network's artificial neurons [stochastic](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stochastic_process "Stochastic process") transfer functions,[[156]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-Ackley1985-158) or by giving them stochastic weights. This makes them useful tools for [optimization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Optimization_(mathematics) "Optimization (mathematics)") problems, since the random fluctuations help the network escape from [local minima](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Maxima_and_minima "Maxima and minima").[[157]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-159) Stochastic neural networks trained using a [Bayesian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayes%27_theorem "Bayes' theorem") approach are known as **Bayesian neural networks**.[[158]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-160)

### Topological deep learning

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Topological deep learning")]

[Topological deep learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topological_deep_learning "Topological deep learning"), first introduced in 2017,[[159]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-161) is an emerging approach in [machine learning](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning "Machine learning") that integrates topology with deep neural networks to address highly intricate and high-order data. Initially rooted in [algebraic topology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algebraic_topology "Algebraic topology"), TDL has since evolved into a versatile framework incorporating tools from other mathematical disciplines, such as [differential topology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Differential_topology "Differential topology") and [geometric topology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geometric_topology "Geometric topology"). As a successful example of mathematical deep learning, TDL continues to inspire advancements in mathematical [artificial intelligence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_intelligence "Artificial intelligence"), fostering a mutually beneficial relationship between AI and [mathematics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics "Mathematics").

### Other

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Other")]

In a [Bayesian](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bayesian_probability "Bayesian probability") framework, a distribution over the set of allowed models is chosen to minimize the cost. [Evolutionary methods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Evolutionary_methods "Evolutionary methods"),[[160]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-162)[gene expression programming](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gene_expression_programming "Gene expression programming"),[[161]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-163)[simulated annealing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simulated_annealing "Simulated annealing"),[[162]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-164)[expectation–maximization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expectation%E2%80%93maximization_algorithm "Expectation–maximization algorithm"), [non-parametric methods](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-parametric_methods "Non-parametric methods") and [particle swarm optimization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Particle_swarm_optimization "Particle swarm optimization")[[163]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-165) are other learning algorithms. Convergent recursion is a learning algorithm for [cerebellar model articulation controller](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerebellar_model_articulation_controller "Cerebellar model articulation controller") (CMAC) neural networks.[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-Qin1-166)[[165]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-Qin2-167)

#### Modes

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Modes")]

![Image 29](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png)This section includes a [list of references](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources"), [related reading](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Further_reading "Wikipedia:Further reading"), or [external links](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links "Wikipedia:External links"), **but its sources remain unclear because it lacks [inline citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")**. Please help [improve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Fact_and_Reference_Check "Wikipedia:WikiProject Fact and Reference Check") this section by [introducing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:When_to_cite "Wikipedia:When to cite") more precise citations._(August 2019)_ _([Learn how and when to remove this message](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Maintenance\_template\_removal "Help:Maintenance template removal"))_

Two modes of learning are available: stochastic and batch. In stochastic learning, each input creates a weight adjustment. In batch learning, weights are adjusted based on a batch of inputs, accumulating errors over the batch. Stochastic learning introduces "noise" into the process, using the local gradient calculated from one data point; this reduces the chance of the network getting stuck in local minima. However, batch learning typically yields a faster, more stable descent to a local minimum, since each update is performed in the direction of the batch's average error. A common compromise is to use "mini-batches", small batches with samples in each batch selected stochastically from the entire data set.

## Types

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=29 "Edit section: Types")]

Main article: [Types of artificial neural networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Types_of_artificial_neural_networks "Types of artificial neural networks")

ANNs have evolved into a broad family of techniques that have advanced the state of the art across multiple domains. The simplest types have one or more static components, including number of units, number of layers, unit weights and [topology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Topology "Topology"). Dynamic types allow one or more of these to evolve via learning. The latter is much more complicated but can shorten learning periods and produce better results. Some types allow/require learning to be "supervised" by the operator, while others operate independently. Some types operate purely in hardware, while others are purely software and run on general purpose computers.

Some of the main breakthroughs include:

*   Convolutional neural networks (CNN) that have proven particularly successful in processing visual and other two-dimensional data;[[166]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-168)[[167]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-lecun2016slides-169) where long short-term memory avoids the [vanishing gradient problem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vanishing_gradient_problem "Vanishing gradient problem")[[168]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:03-170) and can handle signals that have a mix of low and high frequency components aiding large-vocabulary speech recognition,[[169]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-sak2014-171)[[170]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-liwu2015-172)[text-to-speech synthesis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speech_synthesis "Speech synthesis"),[[171]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-173)[[172]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-scholarpedia2-174)[[173]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-zen2015-175) and photo-real talking heads.[[174]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-fan2015-176) Convolutional Neural Networks have also been applied to fraud detection.[[175]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-177)[[176]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-178)
*   Competitive networks such as [generative adversarial networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generative_adversarial_network "Generative adversarial network") in which multiple networks (of varying structure) compete with each other, on tasks such as winning a game[[177]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-preprint-179) or on deceiving the opponent about the authenticity of an input.[[96]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-GANnips-96)

## Network design

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=30 "Edit section: Network design")]

Using artificial neural networks requires an understanding of their characteristics.

*   Choice of model: This depends on the data representation and the application. Model parameters include the number, type, and connectedness of network layers, as well as the size of each and the connection type (full, pooling, etc.). Overly complex models learn slowly.
*   [Learning algorithm](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_learning "Machine learning"): Numerous trade-offs exist between learning algorithms. Almost any algorithm will work well with the correct hyperparameters[[178]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-180) for training on a particular data set. However, selecting and tuning an algorithm for training on unseen data requires significant experimentation.
*   [Robustness](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robustness "Robustness"): If the model, cost function and learning algorithm are selected appropriately, the resulting ANN can become robust.

[Neural architecture search](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_architecture_search "Neural architecture search") (NAS) uses machine learning to automate ANN design. Various approaches to NAS have designed networks that compare well with hand-designed systems. The basic search algorithm is to propose a candidate model, evaluate it against a dataset, and use the results as feedback to teach the NAS network.[[179]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-181) Available systems include [AutoML](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Automated_machine_learning "Automated machine learning") and AutoKeras.[[180]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-182)[scikit-learn library](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scikit-learn "Scikit-learn") provides functions to help with building a deep network from scratch. We can then implement a deep network with [TensorFlow](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/TensorFlow "TensorFlow") or [Keras](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keras "Keras").

Hyperparameters must also be defined as part of the design (they are not learned), governing matters such as how many neurons are in each layer, learning rate, step, stride, depth, receptive field and padding (for CNNs), etc.[[181]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-abs1502.02127-183)The [Python](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Python_(programming_language) "Python (programming language)") code snippet provides an overview of the training function, which uses the training dataset, number of hidden layer units, learning rate, and number of iterations as parameters:[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_]

def train(X, y, n_hidden, learning_rate, n_iter):
 """Training function.

 Args:
 X: Argument X.
 y: Argument y.
 n_hidden: The number of hidden layer units.
 learning_rate: The learning rate.
 n_iter: The number of iterations.

 Returns:
 dict: A dictionary.
 """
    m, n_input = X.shape

    # 1. random initialize weights and biases
    w1 = np.random.randn(n_input, n_hidden)
    b1 = np.zeros((1, n_hidden))
    w2 = np.random.randn(n_hidden, 1)
    b2 = np.zeros((1, 1))

    # 2. in each iteration, feed all layers with the latest weights and biases
    for i in range(n_iter + 1):
        z2 = np.dot(X, w1) + b1
        a2 = sigmoid(z2)
        z3 = np.dot(a2, w2) + b2
        a3 = z3
        dz3 = a3 - y
        dw2 = np.dot(a2.T, dz3)
        db2 = np.sum(dz3, axis=0, keepdims=True)
        dz2 = np.dot(dz3, w2.T) * sigmoid_derivative(z2)
        dw1 = np.dot(X.Y, dz2)
        db1 = np.sum(dz2, axis=0)

        # 3. update weights and biases with gradients
        w1 -= learning_rate * dw1 / m
        w2 -= learning_rate * dw2 / m
        b1 -= learning_rate * db1 / m
        b2 -= learning_rate * db2 / m

        if i % 1000 == 0:
            print("Epoch", i, "loss: ", np.mean(np.square(dz3)))

    model = {"w1": w1, "b1": b1, "w2": w2, "b2": b2}
    return model

## Theoretical properties

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: Theoretical properties")]

### Computational power

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Computational power")]

The [multilayer perceptron](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multilayer_perceptron "Multilayer perceptron") is a [universal function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/UTM_theorem "UTM theorem") approximator, as proven by the [universal approximation theorem](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_approximation_theorem "Universal approximation theorem"). However, the proof is not constructive regarding the number of neurons required, the network topology, the weights and the learning parameters.

A specific recurrent architecture with [rational](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rational_number "Rational number")-valued weights (as opposed to full precision real number-valued weights) has the power of a [universal Turing machine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universal_Turing_machine "Universal Turing machine"),[[182]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-184) using a finite number of neurons and standard linear connections. Further, the use of [irrational](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Irrational_number "Irrational number") values for weights results in a machine with [super-Turing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hypercomputation "Hypercomputation") power.[[183]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-185)[[184]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-186)[_[failed verification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability "Wikipedia:Verifiability")_]

### Capacity

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=33 "Edit section: Capacity")]

A model's "capacity" property corresponds to its ability to model any given function. It is related to the amount of information that can be stored in the network and to the notion of complexity. Two notions of capacity are known by the community. The information capacity and the VC Dimension. The information capacity of a perceptron is intensively discussed in [Sir David MacKay](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_J._C._MacKay "David J. C. MacKay")'s book[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-auto-187) which summarizes work by [Thomas Cover](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_M._Cover "Thomas M. Cover").[[186]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-188) The capacity of a network of standard neurons (not convolutional) can be derived by four rules[[187]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-189) that derive from understanding a neuron as an electrical element. The information capacity captures the functions modelable by the network given any data as input. The second notion, is the [VC dimension](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/VC_dimension "VC dimension"). VC Dimension uses the principles of [measure theory](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Measure_theory "Measure theory") and finds the maximum capacity under the best possible circumstances. This is, given input data in a specific form. As noted in,[[185]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-auto-187) the VC Dimension for arbitrary inputs is half the information capacity of a perceptron. The VC Dimension for arbitrary points is sometimes referred to as Memory Capacity.[[188]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-190)

### Convergence

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=34 "Edit section: Convergence")]

Models may not consistently converge on a single solution, firstly because local minima may exist, depending on the cost function and the model. Secondly, the optimization method used might not guarantee to converge when it begins far from any local minimum. Thirdly, for sufficiently large data or parameters, some methods become impractical.

Another issue worthy to mention is that training may cross some [saddle point](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saddle_point "Saddle point") which may lead the convergence to the wrong direction.

The convergence behavior of certain types of ANN architectures are more understood than others. When the width of network approaches to infinity, the ANN is well described by its first order [Taylor expansion](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Taylor_expansion "Taylor expansion") throughout training, and so inherits the [convergence](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Convergent_series "Convergent series") behavior of [affine models](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_model "Linear model").[[189]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-191)[[190]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-192) Another example is when parameters are small, it is observed that ANNs often fit target functions from low to high frequencies. This behavior is referred to as the spectral bias, or frequency principle, of neural networks.[[191]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-193)[[192]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-194)[[193]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-195)[[194]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-196) This phenomenon is the opposite to the behavior of some well studied iterative numerical schemes such as [Jacobi method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacobi_method "Jacobi method"). Deeper neural networks have been observed to be more biased towards low frequency functions.[[195]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-197)

### Generalization and statistics

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=35 "Edit section: Generalization and statistics")]

![Image 30](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg/40px-Text_document_with_red_question_mark.svg.png)This section includes a [list of references](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources "Wikipedia:Citing sources"), [related reading](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Further_reading "Wikipedia:Further reading"), or [external links](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links "Wikipedia:External links"), **but its sources remain unclear because it lacks [inline citations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources#Inline_citations "Wikipedia:Citing sources")**. Please help [improve](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:WikiProject_Fact_and_Reference_Check "Wikipedia:WikiProject Fact and Reference Check") this section by [introducing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:When_to_cite "Wikipedia:When to cite") more precise citations._(August 2019)_ _([Learn how and when to remove this message](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:Maintenance\_template\_removal "Help:Maintenance template removal"))_

Applications whose goal is to create a system that generalizes well to unseen examples, face the possibility of [over-training](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Overfitting "Overfitting"). This arises in convoluted or over-specified systems when the network capacity significantly exceeds the needed free parameters.

Two approaches address over-training. The first is to use [cross-validation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cross-validation_(statistics) "Cross-validation (statistics)") and similar techniques to check for the presence of over-training and to select hyperparameters to minimize the generalization error. The second is to use some form of _[regularization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regularization\_(mathematics) "Regularization (mathematics)")_. This concept emerges in a probabilistic (Bayesian) framework, where regularization can be performed by selecting a larger prior probability over simpler models; but also in statistical learning theory, where the goal is to minimize over two quantities: the 'empirical risk' and the 'structural risk', which roughly corresponds to the error over the training set and the predicted error in unseen data due to overfitting.

[![Image 31](https://upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Synapse_deployment.jpg/330px-Synapse_deployment.jpg)](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Synapse_deployment.jpg)

Confidence analysis of a neural network

Supervised neural networks that use a [mean squared error](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mean_squared_error "Mean squared error") (MSE) cost function can use formal statistical methods to determine the confidence of the trained model. The MSE on a validation set can be used as an estimate for variance. This value can then be used to calculate the [confidence interval](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confidence_interval "Confidence interval") of network output, assuming a [normal distribution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Normal_distribution "Normal distribution"). A confidence analysis made this way is statistically valid as long as the output [probability distribution](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Probability_distribution "Probability distribution") stays the same and the network is not modified.

By assigning a [softmax activation function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Softmax_activation_function "Softmax activation function"), a generalization of the [logistic function](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logistic_function "Logistic function"), on the output layer of the neural network (or a softmax component in a component-based network) for categorical target variables, the outputs can be interpreted as posterior probabilities. This is useful in classification as it gives a certainty measure on classifications.

The softmax activation function is:

{\displaystyle y_{i}={\frac {e^{x_{i}}}{\sum _{j=1}^{c}e^{x_{j}}}}}![Image 32: {\displaystyle y_{i}={\frac {e^{x_{i}}}{\sum _{j=1}^{c}e^{x_{j}}}}}](https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/481884e3588b192020e8d0aafe16b41c0ed26007)

## Applications

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=36 "Edit section: Applications")]

Artificial neural networks (ANNs) have undergone significant advancements, particularly in their ability to model complex systems, handle large data sets, and adapt to various types of applications. Their evolution over the past few decades has been marked by a broad range of applications in fields such as image processing, speech recognition, natural language processing, finance, and medicine.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:07-198) Artificial neural networks now form the core of many artificial intelligence systems, including natural language processing, computer vision, speech recognition, and autonomous systems.[[197]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-199)

Because of their ability to model and reproduce nonlinear processes, artificial neural networks have found applications in many disciplines. These include:

*   [Function approximation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Function_approximation "Function approximation"),[[198]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-200) or [regression analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Regression_analysis "Regression analysis"),[[199]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-201) (including [time series prediction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Time_series#Prediction_and_forecasting "Time series"), [fitness approximation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Fitness_approximation "Fitness approximation"),[[200]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-202) and modeling)
*   [Data processing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_processing "Data processing")[[201]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-203) (including filtering, clustering, [blind source separation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blind_source_separation "Blind source separation"),[[202]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-204) and compression)
*   [Nonlinear system identification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nonlinear_system_identification "Nonlinear system identification")[[95]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-SAB1-95) and control (including vehicle control, trajectory prediction,[[203]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-205)[adaptive control](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adaptive_control "Adaptive control"), [process control](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Process_control "Process control"), and [natural resource management](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_resource_management "Natural resource management"))
*   [Pattern recognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pattern_recognition "Pattern recognition") (including radar systems, [face identification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Facial_recognition_system "Facial recognition system"), signal classification,[[204]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-206)[novelty detection](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Novelty_detection "Novelty detection"), [3D reconstruction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/3D_reconstruction "3D reconstruction"),[[205]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-207) object recognition, and sequential decision making[[206]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-TurekNeuralNet-208))
*   Sequence recognition (including [gesture](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gesture_recognition "Gesture recognition"), [speech](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speech_recognition "Speech recognition"), and handwritten and printed text recognition[[207]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-209))
*   Sensor data analysis[[208]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-210) (including [image analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Image_analysis "Image analysis"))
*   [Robotics](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robotics "Robotics") (including directing manipulators and [prostheses](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prosthesis "Prosthesis"))
*   [Data mining](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_mining "Data mining") (including [knowledge discovery in databases](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Knowledge_discovery_in_databases "Knowledge discovery in databases"))
*   Finance[[209]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-211) (such as [ex-ante](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ex-ante "Ex-ante") models for specific financial long-run forecasts and [artificial financial markets](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_financial_market "Artificial financial market"))
*   [Quantum chemistry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantum_chemistry "Quantum chemistry")[[210]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-Balabin_2009-212)
*   [General game playing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/General_game_playing "General game playing")[[211]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-213)
*   [Generative AI](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generative_AI "Generative AI")[[212]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-214)
*   [Data visualization](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Data_visualization "Data visualization")
*   [Machine translation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_translation "Machine translation")
*   Social network filtering[[213]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-215)
*   [E-mail spam](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/E-mail_spam "E-mail spam") filtering
*   [Medical diagnosis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medical_diagnosis "Medical diagnosis")[[214]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-Ciaramella-216)

ANNs have been used to diagnose several types of cancers[[215]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-217)[[216]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-218) and to distinguish highly invasive cancer cell lines from less invasive lines using only cell shape information.[[217]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-219)[[218]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-220)

ANNs have been used to accelerate reliability analysis of infrastructures subject to natural disasters[[219]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-221)[[220]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-222) and to predict foundation settlements.[[221]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-223) It can also be useful to mitigate flood by the use of ANNs for modelling rainfall-runoff.[[222]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-224) ANNs have also been used for building black-box models in [geoscience](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geoscience "Geoscience"): [hydrology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hydrology "Hydrology"),[[223]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-225)[[224]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-226) ocean modelling and [coastal engineering](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Coastal_engineering "Coastal engineering"),[[225]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-227)[[226]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-228) and [geomorphology](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Geomorphology "Geomorphology").[[227]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-229) ANNs have been employed in [cybersecurity](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_security "Computer security"), with the objective to discriminate between legitimate activities and malicious ones. For example, machine learning has been used for classifying Android malware,[[228]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-230) for identifying domains belonging to threat actors and for detecting URLs posing a security risk.[[229]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-231) Research is underway on ANN systems designed for penetration testing, for detecting botnets,[[230]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-232) credit cards frauds[[231]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-233) and network intrusions.

ANNs have been proposed as a tool to solve [partial differential equations](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Partial_differential_equation "Partial differential equation") in physics[[232]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-234)[[233]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-235)[[234]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-236) and simulate the properties of many-body [open quantum systems](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Open_quantum_system "Open quantum system").[[235]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-237)[[236]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-238)[[237]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-239)[[238]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-240) In brain research ANNs have studied short-term behavior of [individual neurons](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Biological_neuron_models "Biological neuron models"),[[239]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-241) the dynamics of [neural circuitry](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_circuit "Neural circuit") arise from interactions between individual neurons and how behavior can arise from abstract neural modules that represent complete subsystems. Studies considered long-and short-term plasticity of neural systems and their relation to learning and memory from the individual neuron to the system level.

It is possible to create a profile of a user's interests from pictures, using artificial neural networks trained for object recognition.[[240]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-242)

Beyond their traditional applications, artificial neural networks are increasingly being utilized in interdisciplinary research, such as materials science. For instance, graph neural networks (GNNs) have demonstrated their capability in scaling deep learning for the discovery of new stable materials by efficiently predicting the total energy of crystals. This application underscores the adaptability and potential of ANNs in tackling complex problems beyond the realms of predictive modeling and artificial intelligence, opening new pathways for scientific discovery and innovation.[[241]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-243)

### Image processing

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=37 "Edit section: Image processing")]

In the realm of image processing, ANNs are employed in [computer vision](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_vision "Computer vision") tasks such as image classification, object recognition, and image segmentation. For instance, deep convolutional neural networks (CNNs) have been important in handwritten digit recognition, achieving state-of-the-art performance.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:07-198) This demonstrates the ability of ANNs to effectively process and interpret complex visual information, leading to advancements in fields ranging from automated surveillance to medical imaging.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:07-198)

### Speech recognition

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=38 "Edit section: Speech recognition")]

By modeling speech signals, ANNs are used for tasks like speaker identification and speech-to-text conversion. Deep neural network architectures have introduced significant improvements in large vocabulary continuous [speech recognition](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Speech_recognition "Speech recognition"), outperforming traditional techniques.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:07-198)[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:15-244) These advancements have enabled the development of more accurate and efficient voice-activated systems, enhancing user interfaces in technology products.[[243]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-245)[[244]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-246)

### Natural language processing

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=39 "Edit section: Natural language processing")]

In [natural language processing](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Natural_language_processing "Natural language processing"), ANNs are used for tasks such as [text classification](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Document_classification "Document classification"), [sentiment analysis](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sentiment_analysis "Sentiment analysis"), and [machine translation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Machine_translation "Machine translation"). They have enabled the development of models that can accurately translate between languages, understand the context and sentiment in textual data, and categorize text based on content.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:07-198)[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:15-244) This has implications for automated customer service, content moderation, and language understanding technologies.[[245]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-247)[_[vague](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness "Wikipedia:Vagueness")_]

### Control systems

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=40 "Edit section: Control systems")]

In the domain of control systems, ANNs are used to model dynamic systems for tasks such as system identification, control design, and optimization. For instance, deep feedforward neural networks are important in system identification and control applications.[[246]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-248)[_[vague](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Vagueness "Wikipedia:Vagueness")_]

### Finance

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=41 "Edit section: Finance")]

Further information: [Applications of artificial intelligence §Trading and investment](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Applications_of_artificial_intelligence#Trading_and_investment "Applications of artificial intelligence")

ANNs are used for [stock market prediction](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quantitative_investing "Quantitative investing") and [credit scoring](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Credit_scoring "Credit scoring"):

*   In investing, ANNs can process vast amounts of financial data, recognize complex patterns, and forecast stock market trends, aiding investors and risk managers in making informed decisions.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:07-198)
*   In credit scoring, ANNs offer data-driven, personalized assessments of creditworthiness, improving the accuracy of [default](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Credit_risk "Credit risk") predictions and automating the lending process.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:15-244)[_[better source needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Questionable\_sources "Wikipedia:Verifiability")_]

ANNs require high-quality data and careful tuning, and their "black-box" nature can pose challenges in interpretation.[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:3-249) Nevertheless, ANNs continue to play a role in finance, offering insights and enhancing [risk management strategies](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Financial_risk_management "Financial risk management").[[247]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:3-249)[[248]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-250)[[249]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-251)

### Medicine

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=42 "Edit section: Medicine")]

ANNs are able to process and analyze vast medical datasets. They enhance diagnostic accuracy, especially by interpreting complex [medical imaging](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Medical_imaging "Medical imaging") for early disease detection, and by predicting patient outcomes for personalized treatment planning.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:15-244) In [drug discovery](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Drug_discovery "Drug discovery"), ANNs speed up the identification of potential drug candidates and predict their efficacy and safety, significantly reducing development time and costs.[[196]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:07-198) Additionally, their application in [personalized medicine](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Personalized_medicine "Personalized medicine") and healthcare data analysis allows tailored therapies and efficient patient care management.[[242]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:15-244) Ongoing research is aimed at addressing remaining challenges such as data privacy and model interpretability, as well as expanding the scope of ANN applications in medicine.[[250]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-252)

### Cybersecurity

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=43 "Edit section: Cybersecurity")]

Neural networks are widely applied in cybersecurity for tasks such as anomaly detection, malware classification, and intrusion detection. By learning patterns of normal system or network behavior, neural models can identify deviations that may indicate malicious activity.[[251]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-253)

### Content creation

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=44 "Edit section: Content creation")]

ANNs such as [generative adversarial networks](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Generative_adversarial_network "Generative adversarial network") and [transformers](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transformer_(machine_learning_model) "Transformer (machine learning model)") are used for [content creation](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Content_creation "Content creation") across numerous industries.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:09-254) Deep learning models are able to learn the style of an artist or musician from huge datasets and generate completely new artworks and music compositions. For instance, [DALL-E](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DALL-E "DALL-E") is a deep neural network trained on 650 million pairs of images and texts across the internet that can create artworks based on text entered by the user.[[253]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-255) In the field of music, transformers have been used to create original music for commercials and documentaries through companies such as [AIVA](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/AIVA "AIVA") and [Jukedeck](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jukedeck "Jukedeck").[[254]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-256) In the marketing industry, generative models have been used to create personalized advertisements for consumers.[[252]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-:09-254) Additionally, major film companies are partnering with technology companies to analyze the financial success of a film, such as the partnership between [Warner Bros](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Warner_Bros. "Warner Bros.") and technology company Cinelytic established in 2020.[[255]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-257)[_[importance?](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:What\_Wikipedia\_is\_not#Encyclopedic\_content "Wikipedia:What Wikipedia is not")_] Furthermore, neural networks have found uses in video game creation, where [non-player characters](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Non-player_character "Non-player character") can make decisions based on all the characters currently in the game.[[256]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-258)

## Criticism

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=45 "Edit section: Criticism")]

### Training

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=46 "Edit section: Training")]

A common criticism of neural networks, particularly in robotics, is that they require too many training samples for real-world operation.[[257]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-259) Any learning machine needs sufficient representative examples in order to capture the underlying structure that allows it to generalize to new cases. Potential solutions include randomly shuffling training examples, by using a numerical optimization algorithm that does not take too large steps when changing the network connections following an example, grouping examples in so-called mini-batches and/or introducing a recursive least squares algorithm for [CMAC](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cerebellar_model_articulation_controller "Cerebellar model articulation controller").[[164]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-Qin1-166) Dean Pomerleau uses a neural network to train a robotic vehicle to drive on multiple types of roads (single lane, multi-lane, dirt, etc.), and a large amount of his research is devoted to extrapolating multiple training scenarios from a single training experience, and preserving past training diversity so that the system does not become overtrained (if, for example, it is presented with a series of right turns—it should not learn to always turn right).[[258]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-260)[_[needs copy edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Basic\_copyediting "Wikipedia:Basic copyediting")_]

### Theory

[[edit](https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Neural_network_(machine_learning)&action=edit&section=47 "Edit section: Theory")]

A central claim[_[citation needed](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation\_needed "Wikipedia:Citation needed")_] of ANNs is that they embody new and powerful general principles for processing information. These principles are [ill-defined](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ill-defined "Ill-defined"). This allows simple statistical association (the basic function of artificial neural networks) to be described as learning or recognition. In 1997, [Alexander Dewdney](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alexander_Dewdney "Alexander Dewdney"), a former _[Scientific American](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scientific\_American "Scientific American")_ columnist, commented that as a result, artificial neural networks have a

> something-for-nothing quality, one that imparts a peculiar aura of laziness and a distinct lack of curiosity about just how good these computing systems are. No human hand (or mind) intervenes; solutions are found as if by magic; and no one, it seems, has learned anything.[[259]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-261)

One response to Dewdney is that neural networks have been successfully used to handle many complex and diverse tasks, ranging from autonomously flying aircraft[[260]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-262) to detecting credit card fraud to mastering the game of [Go](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Go_(game) "Go (game)").

Technology writer Roger Bridgman commented:

> Neural networks, for instance, are in the dock not only because they have been hyped to high heaven, (what hasn't?) but also because you could create a successful net without understanding how it worked: the bunch of numbers that captures its behaviour would in all probability be "an opaque, unreadable table...valueless as a scientific resource".
> 
> 
> In spite of his emphatic declaration that science is not technology, Dewdney seems here to pillory neural nets as bad science when most of those devising them are just trying to be good engineers. An unreadable table that a useful machine could read would still be well worth having.[[261]](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Neural_network_(machine_learning)#cite_note-263)

Although it is true that analyzing what has been learned by an artificial neural network is difficult, it is much easier to do so than to analyze what has been learned by a biological neural network.
